I have ALWAYS wanted to visit different areas of Japan, not just the popular areas for tourists- but the less travelled areas too. I want to talk to people and see the untouched beauty of a culturally saturated archipelago. I want to try the food, especially the food lovingly made by generations of families who haven't moved much from their particular area- and experience what day-to-day life is there outside of [but still including] things like tourist traps or the idealized western versions of what most people think Japan is.   Though I know I idealize it myself a little- I do want to see the pros and the cons of life. It's really the only way to truly appreciate it.  Maybe someday! As it stands i'm FAR too poor, but i'm planning a visit once I have more money and can speak/read the language better.  It's only right to make sure I am prepared and educated before I step foot anywhere that isn't my home land.

Sadly, I don't think you can recapture the feeling of the original Journey Across Japan, without the biking element, or something that can appropriately replace it. The main appeal of the original series, for me at least, was the actual journeying aspect; the slow and steady progress from place to place, the fact that progress was made solely by your body's ability to carry on, and just being with you as you felt the wind on your face, struggled with the hills, braved the weather, and conversed with whichever biking partner you had at the time. Those portions were where the magic was for me, with the cities, challenges, and the (short-lived) daily videos just being icing on the cake. None of the other Journey Across Japan series managed to capture that same genuine feeling of adventure for me, specifically because they lacked that focus on how to actually make the journey.

"The bigger you get as a creator, the further away you get from your audience." It's a reality, it's inescapable, but I've always felt that it's a shame that creators distance themselves from the people who made their success possible. And that's one of the things that makes Chris stand out. He's not only an affable gent, but he's humble enough to see this reality and understand it and recognize it - when you start with a wonky camera and an idea, and you get 3 views, 10 views. 100, views, and you persevere, and one day you're at almost 3 million subscribers...and you don't forget those 100 views that you started with and built off of.  And Chris doesn't.  Never get too big for the people whose support got you where you are.  Cheers, Chris, and have a blast!
